❯ Use the following research on deck primers to update our ai sidecar app. It   
  is currently not working, so needs a complete overhaul. It was built off of   
  draftsim having consistent primer structures, but that turned out to not be   
  the case. Here is the research, use this to overhaul the deck primer          
  ingestion system: # Primer Sources for an MTG AI Sidecar Knowledge Base       
                                                                                
  ## What the research says                                                     
                                                                                
  The biggest practical issue is not finding *any* primers. It is finding       
  primers that are still valid after recent bans, unbans, set releases, and     
  metagame pivots. As of **May 18, 2026**, Wizards made no changes to Standard, 
   Vintage, Historic, Timeless, or Brawl, but it **banned Cori-Steel Cutter in  
  Pioneer**, **banned Phlage, Titan of Fire’s Fury and Lotus Field and unbanned 
   Violent Outburst and Umezawa’s Jitte in Modern**, **banned Undercity         
  Informer in Legacy**, and **unbanned Bonder’s Ornament in Pauper**; Wizards   
  also set the **next announcement for June 30, 2026**. Earlier, on **February  
  9, 2026**, Wizards had already made a large Historic update, banning Eldrazi  
  Temple, Ajani, Nacatl Pariah, Crop Rotation, and Scholar of the Lost Trove    
  while unbanning several cards including Force of Negation, Endurance,         
  Wilderness Reclamation, and Agent of Treachery. Any knowledge base that       
  ignores those dates will ingest primers that are already stale on arrival.    
  citeturn40view0turn39view0                                                
                                                                                
  There is also no single source on the public internet that gives you a        
  uniform primer template across **Standard, Modern, Pioneer, Legacy, Vintage,  
  Historic, Pauper, and Premodern**. The ecosystem is fragmented across several 
   source types: **Metafy** has highly structured paid guides that explicitly   
  advertise matchup guides, sideboard notes, and even mulligan guidance;        
  **Cards Realm** publishes recurring “Deck Tech & Sideboard Guide” articles    
  across many target formats; **MTG Arena Zone** is especially strong on        
  current Historic deep-dives; **The EPIC Storm** offers date-stamped paid      
  sideboard guides in PDF and Google Sheet form for combo decks across Legacy,  
  Vintage, Modern, Pioneer, and Pauper; **Hareruya** has pro-authored longform  
  guides with content tables and matchup sections; **Premodern Magic** is the   
  community-specific hub for Premodern rules and deck tech; and **Moxfield**    
  exposes dedicated `/primer` pages that are useful as a fallback community     
  source when editorial coverage is thin. citeturn37view0turn42view0turn42v 
  iew4turn36search1turn13view0turn24search1turn25sear                       
  ──── (53 lines hidden) ────────────────────────────────────────────────────── 
  fied. If a Pauper primer assumes **Bonder’s Ornament** is unavailable, it     
  does not necessarily become useless, but it should be earmarked for           
  re-review. citeturn40view0turn39view0                                     
                                                                                
  ## The best starting corpus                                                   
                                                                                
  If I were building the first serious version of this knowledge base today, I  
  would start with a **curated ingestion set**, not a giant scrape. The best    
  opening stack is **Metafy for Standard**, **Cards Realm for broad             
  multi-format coverage**, **MTG Arena Zone for Historic**, **The EPIC Storm    
  for exact sideboard matrices in combo decks**, **Hareruya for pro-authored    
  Modern and Pioneer longform guides**, and **Premodern Magic plus MTGDecks     
  plus a few strong 2026 Premodern articles** for the fan-run format. That      
  combination gives you much better coverage of the fields you care             
  about—mulligans, sequencing, matchup notes, and sideboarding—than trying to   
  bulk index metagame pages or user decklists first.                            
  citeturn37view0turn42view0turn42view4turn36search1turn14view0turn24sea 
  rch1turn24search4turn42view6                                               
                                                                                
  If the project priority is **uniform parsing**, the order should be:          
  **Metafy**, **Cards Realm**, **The EPIC Storm**, **MTG Arena Zone**, then     
  **Hareruya**, and finally **Moxfield** as a gap-filler. If the project        
  priority is **maximum format breadth**, the order should be: **Cards Realm**, 
   **The EPIC Storm**, **MTG Arena Zone**, **Premodern Magic**, **Ultimate      
  Guard’s 2026 Pauper/Premodern pieces**, then **Metafy** for the most valuable 
   Standard decks. In practice, the strongest long-term architecture is to use  
  those primer sources for tactical guidance and pair them with **Untapped**,   
  **MTGGoldfish**, **Magic.gg**, and **MTGDecks** as your freshness and         
  archetype-priority layer. citeturn42view0turn36search1turn42view4turn24s 
  earch1turn42view3turn26search14turn37view0turn7search11turn41search0tur 
  n41search1turn41search2turn41search3turn41search11turn24search4          
                                                                                
  The short version is that the internet *does* offer enough current primer     
  material to build a strong MTG sidecar knowledge base, but the winning        
  strategy is not “find one perfect source.” It is to combine a few             
  **high-structure primer sources** with a separate **metagame freshness        
  layer**, and to store every extracted fact with a format, archetype, date,    
  and confidence tag. That will let the sidecar answer the questions players    
  actually ask—what hands to keep, how to sequence a weak hand, what your role  
  is in a matchup, and how to sideboard today rather than three bans ago.

      decks rotate out of the meta? Do we keep them in an archive somewhere?

     Deck Primer Ingestion Overhaul

     Context

     The sidecar's piloting-guide ingestion was built around an assumption that
     Draftsim publishes primers with a consistent HTML template across all 
     archetypes. The research summary shows this is false: only 4 of ~60 Modern
     archetypes resolved successfully because Draftsim uses several undocumented
      URL patterns and at least two different content templates (semantic
     <article> vs <div class="entry-content">). The result is a knowledge base
     where most archetypes fall through to the LLM's training data, which is
     increasingly stale relative to 2026 bans (Phlage / Lotus Field / Cori-Steel
      Cutter / Undercity Informer banned, Violent Outburst / Jitte / Bonder's
     Ornament unbanned, Historic reset on 2026-02-09,
     Modern/Pioneer/Legacy/Pauper changes on 2026-05-18).

     The fix is to (1) replace Draftsim-as-primary with a multi-provider 
     ingestion pipeline keyed off Cards Realm, Hareruya, MTG Arena Zone, and
     Moxfield, with Draftsim demoted to a last-resort source; (2) extract
     structured fields via the builder LLM operating on cleaned HTML rather than
      rigid heading-based parsing; (3) extend the schema with provenance, 
     confidence, and freshness metadata so a guide that references a banned card
      is still useful — just flagged; (4) tie the build queue to the metagame 
     scrape so new archetypes get primers automatically and rotated-out decks
     are archived rather than deleted; and (5) synthesize a default primer with
     the builder LLM when no editorial source exists, marked as inferred with
     low confidence.

     This unblocks recognize, identify-own-archetype, and downstream advice
     generation for the long tail of archetypes that currently get only the
     midrange-generic fallback.

     Critical files

     Modify:
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/draftsim.py — demote to a provider plugin
      under the new primers/sources/ package; preserve URL patterns and
     parse_sections as the Draftsim-specific parser used only when LLM
     extraction is disabled
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/builder_llm.py — add
     extract_primer_fields(cleaned_text, archetype, fmt, source_meta) returning
     structured JSON; reuses existing BUILDER_LLM_BASE_URL/MODEL_NAME env config
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/piloting_schema.py — extend models with
     Provenance, FieldEvidence, LegalEra, StalenessFlags, decklist_hash; bump
     PILOTING_SCHEMA_VERSION to 2; add migration shim so existing v1 guides
     still load
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/piloting.py — update loader to handle
     v1/v2, read _archive/ subdir, attach computed staleness flags at load time,
      expose archive guides via available_guides()
     - forge-llm-sidecar/scripts/build_piloting_guides.py — orchestrate the
     multi-source chain; add --source flag, --rebuild-archived, and queue-mode
     that consumes the metagame diff
     - forge-llm-sidecar/scripts/scrape_metagame.py — after writing new metagame
      JSON, emit metagame_data/<fmt>.diff.json with {new_archetypes, 
     dropped_archetypes, returned_archetypes} for the builder to consume
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/main.py:131-165 — /piloting debug endpoint to
     include provenance + stale flags in its response

     Create:
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/primers/__init__.py
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/primers/sources/base.py — Provider ABC
     with search(archetype, fmt) -> list[Candidate] and fetch(candidate) -> 
     RawPrimer
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/primers/sources/cards_realm.py — primary
     source; URL search via site-specific Google CSE or direct URL guessing;
     sectioned-page parser (Cards Realm consistently exposes The Decklist /
     Sideboard Guide h2/h3 blocks per the research)
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/primers/sources/hareruya.py —
     pro-authored longform; parses Contents block + matchup sections
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/primers/sources/mtg_arena_zone.py —
     strongest for Historic; lists archetype guides on a per-format index page
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/primers/sources/moxfield.py — fallback
     when editorial coverage is thin; hits moxfield.com/decks/.../primer
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/primers/sources/draftsim.py — thin
     wrapper over the existing module; used only as final fallback
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/primers/clean_html.py —
     clean_for_extraction(html) -> str: strips
     script/style/nav/aside/form/footer/header/iframe, removes class-blacklist
     (ads, sidebar, related, comments, breadcrumbs, newsletter), preserves h1-h4
      and p/li/table content as plain text with heading markers (### Sideboard 
     Guide). Reused by every provider.
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/primers/orchestrator.py —
     build_primer(archetype, fmt) -> PilotingGuide: walks the provider chain
     (per-format priority list), invokes builder_llm.extract_primer_fields,
     falls back to a default_primer synthesis when no provider returns content,
     and merges provenance into the result
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/primers/default_primer.py — LLM-only
     synthesis using deck name + signature cards + colors + format meta-context;
      output gets confidence: 0.3 and inferred: true on every text field
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/banlist_events.json — hand-curated event
     log; entries {date, format, banned: [...], unbanned: [...], note} seeded
     with the 2026-02-09 Historic reset and the 2026-05-18 multi-format
     announcement
     - forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/piloting/archive/<format>/<slug>.json —
     rotated-out archetypes (loader still reads them, but available_guides()
     separates live vs archive)

     Tests to add:
     - forge-llm-sidecar/tests/test_primer_providers.py — fixture HTML for each
     source, asserts clean_for_extraction output and the resulting PilotingGuide
     - forge-llm-sidecar/tests/test_primer_orchestrator.py — provider chain with
      mocked HTTP; verifies fallback ordering, default-primer synthesis, schema
     validation
     - forge-llm-sidecar/tests/test_staleness.py — given a guide referencing
     Phlage with generated_at before 2026-05-18 and format: modern, asserts
     stale_flags.banned_cards_referenced == ["Phlage, Titan of Fire's Fury"]

     Design details

     1. Provider chain (per-format priority)

     modern:    hareruya -> cards_realm -> moxfield -> draftsim ->
     default_primer
     pioneer:   cards_realm -> hareruya -> moxfield -> draftsim ->
     default_primer
     standard:  cards_realm -> moxfield -> draftsim -> default_primer
     historic:  mtg_arena_zone -> cards_realm -> moxfield -> default_primer
     legacy:    cards_realm -> moxfield -> draftsim -> default_primer
     pauper:    cards_realm -> moxfield -> draftsim -> default_primer
     vintage:   cards_realm -> moxfield -> default_primer
     premodern: moxfield -> default_primer

     A provider is "successful" when LLM extraction yields a non-empty overview
     AND at least one of {key_cards, matchups, game_plan.*}. Otherwise the
     orchestrator falls through to the next provider.

     2. LLM extraction prompt (in builder_llm.extract_primer_fields)

     System: "You are extracting structured piloting guidance from a Magic: The 
     Gathering primer article. Ground every field in the supplied text. For each
      field, mark it 'explicit' if the article directly states it, 'inferred' if
      you derived it from context. Never invent cards. Respond with a single 
     JSON object."

     User message includes: archetype name, format, source URL + publisher, the
     cleaned text (capped at ~12k chars; truncated tail-first with a marker),
     the target JSON schema (matching extended PilotingGuide).

     Reuses existing BUILDER_LLM_BASE_URL / BUILDER_LLM_API_KEY /
     BUILDER_MODEL_NAME. No request-path impact.

     3. Extended schema (v2)

     Added to PilotingGuide:
     - provenance: list[Provenance] — one entry per source consulted (publisher,
      author, source_url, publish_date, fetched_at, http_status,
     used_for_fields)
     - legal_era: LegalEra — br_window_start: date, br_window_end: date | null,
     set_legality_snapshot: [str]
     - decklist_hash: str | null — SHA-256 of sorted canonicalized signature
     cards; lets the loader detect when the same archetype name now means a
     different deck
     - stale_flags: StalenessFlags — computed at load time, not stored verbatim:
      banned_cards_referenced, unbanned_cards_missing, format_rotation_event,
     out_of_meta

     Each text-bearing field gains an optional FieldEvidence sibling (e.g.
     overview_evidence, mulligan.keep_criteria_evidence[i]) holding {confidence:
      0-1, kind: "explicit"|"inferred", source_index: int}. Default
     schema-version-1 loaders just fill these with {confidence: 0.7, kind: 
     "inferred", source_index: 0} so old guides keep working.

     4. Staleness, not deletion

     The loader computes stale_flags by:
     1. Loading banlist_events.json; finding all events with date > 
     guide.metadata.generated_at in the guide's format.
     2. Building two sets: banned_after = ∪ banned, unbanned_after = ∪ unbanned.
     3. banned_cards_referenced = banned_after ∩ (key_cards.name ∪ 
     win_conditions ∪ matchups.watch_for ∪ tokens(overview)).
     4. format_rotation_event = bool(events with type=='rotation' or |banned ∪ 
     unbanned| >= 3).

     Out-of-date primers are still served — the recognize and advice prompts get
      an additional system note: "This guide was written 2026-04-15. Since then,
      Phlage was banned and Jitte was unbanned. Treat references to those cards 
     accordingly." (string is built deterministically by game_advisor.py from
     stale_flags; no extra LLM call).

     5. Metagame-driven build queue

     scrape_metagame.py already writes metagame_data/<fmt>.json. We add: before
     overwriting, load the prior file, compute set differences on archetype
     names, and write <fmt>.diff.json next to it.

     build_piloting_guides.py gains --from-diff which:
     - For each new_archetype → run full provider chain.
     - For each dropped_archetype → if a guide exists under
     piloting/<fmt>/<slug>.json, move it to piloting/<fmt>/_archive/<slug>.json.
     - For each returned_archetype (in diff but already archived) → move it
     back.
     - Refresh any guide whose metadata.generated_at is older than the format's
     TTL (Standard/Historic: 30d, Modern/Pioneer/Legacy/Pauper: 90d, Vintage:
     180d, Premodern: 365d).

     CI/cron flow: weekly scrape → diff → build runs in --from-diff mode →
     commit if guides changed.

     6. Default-primer synthesis

     When all editorial providers fail, default_primer.synthesize(archetype, 
     fmt, signature_cards, colors) calls the builder LLM with a
     heavily-constrained prompt: only allow cards from the supplied list or
     commonly-named staples for the format. Output gets provenance = 
     [{publisher: "builder_llm_default", ...}], every FieldEvidence.kind = 
     "inferred", every confidence ≤ 0.4. The recognize-prompt formatter will
     display this prominently so the runtime model knows it's working from
     synthesized rather than sourced material.

     This is the foundation for the user's future "primer-builder agent" idea —
     once we have a corpus of well-extracted guides, that corpus can become the
     fine-tuning set for a stronger default-primer model. Out of scope for this
     overhaul, but the data model supports it.

     7. Out of scope (noted for future work)

     - Pro game-log ingestion (the user asked about it) — would feed
     sequencing_tips and mulligan.examples from real play data; needs a separate
      ingestion pipeline against MTGO/Arena replay sources and is its own
     project.
     - Fine-tuned primer-builder LLM — depends on having a clean corpus first.
     - Paid sources (Metafy, EPIC Storm) — both require authentication and TOS
     review; if added later they slot into the provider chain as additional
     plugins.

     Verification

     1. Unit tests: cd forge-llm-sidecar && uv run pytest 
     tests/test_primer_providers.py tests/test_primer_orchestrator.py 
     tests/test_staleness.py tests/test_piloting.py -v — all green.
     2. Schema migration: load every existing piloting/**/*.json through the v2
     loader; none should fail validation (the v1→v2 shim fills defaults).
     3. End-to-end primer build (offline, with local LLM running):
       - uv run python scripts/scrape_metagame.py modern to refresh and emit a
     diff.
       - uv run python scripts/build_piloting_guides.py modern --archetype 
     "Boros Energy" --force — confirm it now resolves via Cards Realm or
     Hareruya (check metadata.provenance[0].publisher), produces a populated
     guide, validates.
       - Repeat for "Amulet Titan", "Living End", "Domain Zoo" to confirm
     provider chain handles different sources.
     4. Staleness: manually edit a guide's metadata.generated_at to 2026-04-01,
     then curl 
     http://localhost:8765/piloting?archetype=Boros%20Energy&format=modern —
     response should include stale_flags.banned_cards_referenced listing Phlage.
     5. Runtime integration:
       - Start the sidecar (scripts/forge-sidecar.service or uv run uvicorn 
     app.main:app).
       - curl -X POST /identify-own-archetype -d '{"deck": [...Boros Energy 
     list...], "format": "modern"}' — confirm archetype match + guide returned.
       - curl -X POST /recognize -d '{...}' — confirm
     game_advisor.py:_format_guide includes the stale-flag note in the prompt
     when applicable (verify via log).
     6. Default-primer fallback: point the builder at a deliberately-nonexistent
      archetype (--archetype "Test Synth Deck") — confirm
     default_primer.synthesize runs and produces a schema-valid guide with kind:
      "inferred" evidence.
     7. Archive flow: simulate a metagame drop by removing an archetype from
     metagame_data/modern.json and re-running --from-diff; confirm its guide
     moves to piloting/modern/_archive/.

          +list)

      123 +    out_of_meta: bool = False                                 
      124 +    age_days: int = 0                                         
      125 +    notes: list[str] = Field(default_factory=list)            
      126 +                                                              
      127 +                                                              
      128  class GuideMetadata(BaseModel):
      129      """Provenance for a guide (who/what generated it, when).""
           "
      130  
     ...
      150      matchups: list[MatchupNote] = Field(default_factory=list)
      151      common_threats: list[str] = Field(default_factory=list)
      152      metadata: GuideMetadata = Field(default_factory=GuideMetad
           ata)
      153 +

      155 +    provenance: list[Provenance] = Field(default_factory=list)
      156 +    legal_era: LegalEra = Field(default_factory=LegalEra)     
      157 +    decklist_hash: Optional[str] = None                       
      158 +    overview_evidence: Optional[FieldEvidence] = None         
      159 +    win_conditions_evidence: list[FieldEvidence] = Field(defau
          +lt_factory=list)                                              
      160 +    sequencing_tips_evidence: list[FieldEvidence] = Field(defa
          +ult_factory=list)                                             
      161 +    common_threats_evidence: list[FieldEvidence] = Field(defau
          +lt_factory=list)                                              
      162 +                                                              
      163 +    # Computed at load time by the piloting loader; not persis
          +ted to disk.

          +essFlags)                                                     
      165 +                                                              
      166 +                                                              
      167 +def upgrade_v1_payload(raw: dict) -> dict:                    
      168 +    """Patch a v1 guide dict so it round-trips through the v2 
          +model.                                                        
      169 +                                                              
      170 +    Mutates ``raw`` in place and returns it. Idempotent — call
          +ing on a v2 guide                                             
      171 +    leaves it alone. The loader runs this before model_validat
          +e so existing                                                 
      172 +    files keep loading without on-disk migration.             
      173 +    """                                                       
      174 +    if not isinstance(raw, dict):                             
      175 +        return raw                                            
      176 +    meta = raw.get("metadata") or {}                          
      177 +    version = meta.get("schema_version", 1) if isinstance(meta
          +, dict) else 1                                                
      178 +    if version >= PILOTING_SCHEMA_VERSION:                    
      179 +        return raw                                            
      180 +                                                              
      181 +    raw.setdefault("provenance", [])                          
      182 +    raw.setdefault("legal_era", {})                           
      183 +    raw.setdefault("decklist_hash", None)                     
      184 +    raw.setdefault("win_conditions_evidence", [])             
      185 +    raw.setdefault("sequencing_tips_evidence", [])            
      186 +    raw.setdefault("common_threats_evidence", [])             
      187 +    raw.setdefault("overview_evidence", None)                 
      188 +    # Stamp it as v2 in the in-memory copy; we do NOT rewrite 
          +the file on disk.                                             
      189 +    if isinstance(meta, dict):                                
      190 +        meta["schema_version"] = PILOTING_SCHEMA_VERSION      
      191 +        raw["metadata"] = meta                                
      192 +    return raw

  token budgets it spends its budget thinking and emits empty content. The first
   error ("Server disconnected") was likely the server going OOM mid-generation.

      214 +def _coerce_to_schema(raw: dict) -> None:                     
      215 +    """Normalize common LLM shape mistakes in place.          
      216 +                                                              
      217 +    Local models freelance the JSON shape: strings where lists
          + belong,                                                      
      218 +    capitalized enums, plain card names where ``KeyCard`` obje
          +cts are                                                       
      219 +    required, etc. We coerce the easy cases here so the orches
          +trator can

● Here's a quality review of four guides — two sourced from Cards Realm articles
   (highest quality), two from the LLM-synthesis fallback (when no editorial
  source is found):

  Quality Assessment

  ✅ Cards Realm-sourced (Boros Energy, Amulet Titan)

  Strengths:
  - Concrete archetype-specific cards (Amped Raptor, Phelia Exuberant Shepherd,
  Cultivator Colossus, Urza's Saga)
  - Matchups name real opposing archetypes (Mono Black Evoke, Bant Nadu, Golgari
   Yawgmoth) with specific sideboard moves ("Side in Disruptor Flute and Wrath
  of the Skies", "Cut Arboreal Grazer since blocking is unimportant")
  - Sequencing tips reference real mechanical interactions ("Blink Amped Raptor
  with Phelia to generate energy for triggering Guide of Souls on the following
  turn")
  - Win conditions are concrete plays, not abstract goals
  - Common threats name specific opposing cards (Yawgmoth, Primeval Titan,
  Ragavan, Ledger Shredder)

  Weakness:
  - Mulligan keeps/ships are empty — Cards Realm articles often don't include
  explicit mulligan prose, and the extractor doesn't infer when fields are
  missing. The schema accepts empty lists so validation passes, but this is a
  real coverage gap.

  ⚠️ LLM-synthesis fallback (Living End, Izzet Prowess)

  Strengths:
  - Real card names from signature_cards (Force of Negation, Subtlety,
  Cori-Steel Cutter, Mishra's Bauble)
  - Well-populated mulligan keeps/ships
  - Coherent game-plan phases with archetype-specific advice ("Sacrifice Baubles
   for flying prowess tokens to bypass blockers")

  Weaknesses:
  - Matchups are generic categories ("Aggro", "Control", "Midrange") rather than
   named archetypes — synthesis has no metagame context
  - Common threats are abstract ("Counterspells", "Board wipes") rather than
  specific cards
  - Win conditions slightly more abstract than sourced versions

  Two improvements I'd suggest

  1. Inject metagame archetype names into default_primer prompt so synthesized
  matchups name real decks ("vs Boros Energy", "vs Amulet Titan") instead of
  generic "vs Aggro".
  2. Require mulligan inference in the extractor prompt — when the source
  article doesn't explicitly cover mulligans, ask the LLM to infer them from the
   keys cards listed (mark kind: "inferred").

  Want me to implement both, then re-run? Or are you OK with the current quality
   and want me to just wait for the build to finish and move on to other
  formats?

● 50/60 — build is grinding through, no recent errors. ~10 to go.

  YouTube transcript scraping as a piloting source — yes, worth pursuing

  Short answer: yes, this is the highest-leverage missing input for exactly the
  fields we're currently weakest on — sequencing decisions, matchup-specific
  in-game reasoning, and mulligan walkthroughs. Editorial primers tell you what
  to do; gameplay videos tell you why and when.

  What's actually IN those transcripts

  For a typical 30–60 min match video:
  - Mulligan thought process: "Two lands, Phlage, Ragavan, two removal. I keep —
   Ragavan on one is the play, removal protects him on two"
  - Sequencing decisions in real time: "I could cast Phelia now but I want to
  bait the removal first — I'll lead with Guide of Souls and see if they spend
  Solitude on it"
  - Matchup-specific tactics: "Against Living End the line is to keep Force of
  Negation up on turn three even if it means skipping a tempo play"
  - Sideboard reasoning game-by-game: "Game two I'm cutting two Helix and
  bringing in Surgical because their plan post-board is the Living End hardcast
  loop"

  That's exactly the kind of advice that doesn't appear in cards-realm.com deck
  techs.

  Feasibility check

  ┌───────────────┬─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  │    Concern    │                         Reality                         │
  ├───────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Transcript    │ youtube-transcript-api Python lib — no API key, just    │
  │ access        │ video ID. English auto-captions exist on >95% of MTG    │
  │               │ gameplay videos.                                        │
  ├───────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │               │ YouTube Data API v3 (free, 10k units/day = enough for   │
  │ Discovery     │ ~100 channel scans). Channel-restricted search by title │
  │               │  keyword catches most relevant videos.                  │
  ├───────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │               │ We're reading public captions, not redistributing       │
  │ ToS           │ video. Fair for research/personal use; we should NOT    │
  │               │ republish transcript verbatim, just extract heuristics  │
  │               │ from them.                                              │
  ├───────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Recency / B&R │ Easy: filter to videos uploaded after the most recent   │
  │  relevance    │ B&R for the format (Modern: post-2026-05-18).           │
  ├───────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Caption       │ Auto-captions mangle card names ("Phlage" → "flog",     │
  │ errors        │ "Goryo" → "gorillo"). Need LLM cleanup pass that        │
  │               │ cross-references against known signature cards.         │
  ├───────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Filler /      │ First 60s and last 60s often skippable. Chunk by        │
  │ sponsor reads │ timestamp; LLM filters signal.                          │
  ├───────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Per-creator   │ One creator's preference isn't truth — but aggregating  │
  │ bias          │ across 2-3 creators per archetype averages it out.      │
  └───────────────┴─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

  Creators worth targeting

  You named three; here's my expanded list with what each one's best for:

  - Aspiringspike — Modern/Standard ladder grinder, extremely verbal about
  sequencing & mulligans
  - Crokeyz — Pioneer specialist, deep matchup analysis
  - Jim Davis — Modern, very explicit about line trees ("if they have X, I do Y,
   otherwise Z")
  - Reid Duke / CFB content — high-skill commentary on Modern, Legacy
  - AndreaMengucci — Modern, multilingual; clear thought process
  - mengu / DotPMtg / SpikeyMikey13 — Modern competitive
  - NumotTheNummy (Patrick Chapin) — more strategy theory than pure gameplay
  - Saffron Olive (MTGGoldfish) — broad format coverage, good for deeper format
  breadth (Pauper, Legacy, Premodern)
  - PleasantKenobi — Modern + Premodern (helps with the format with weakest
  editorial coverage)
  - LSV (CFB) — mostly Limited, lower priority for constructed primers
  - Pro Tour / MagicCon official — feature matches with two-commentator analysis
   (gold but lower coverage per archetype)

  Architecture — enrichment layer, not primary provider

  This shouldn't be just "another provider in the chain" — it doesn't produce
  primers, it produces gameplay heuristics. My recommendation is an enrichment 
  phase that runs AFTER the orchestrator builds the structural primer:

  1. orchestrator.build_primer(archetype, fmt)        →  structural primer from
  Cards Realm/etc
  2. youtube_enricher.enrich(guide, archetype, fmt)   →  pulls 2-3 gameplay
  videos, extracts
                                                         sequencing + mulligan +
   matchup advice,
                                                         merges into guide with
  provenance entries

  This way:
  - A guide with Cards Realm + 2 YouTube transcripts keeps the structured
  matchup matrix from CR and adds the "why" from the videos
  - Each piece of advice has its own provenance entry showing which video it
  came from + timestamp
  - Adds a new FieldEvidence kind: "gameplay_observed" (between explicit and
  inferred — it's explicit reasoning but from a single play, not a general
  claim)

  Practical scope

  A first build would:
  - Hard-code ~6 channels (the ones above I'm most confident about)
  - For each archetype in the metagame, search those channels for recent videos
  titled {format} {archetype} (allowing fuzzy variants)
  - Pick top 2 by view count + recency
  - Pull transcript
  - Hand to LLM with a focused prompt: "From this MTG gameplay transcript,
  extract concrete piloting heuristics — mulligan rules, sequencing rules,
  matchup-specific tactics. Output JSON with the same fields as a piloting
  guide. Mark each with the timestamp range it came from."
  - Merge into existing guide

  Hidden upside

  Once you have a corpus of (archetype, transcript-extracted heuristics) pairs,
  that's training data for the user's earlier "primer-builder agent" idea. The
  current default_primer is generic because it has no game-state grounding; a
  model fine-tuned on transcript-extracted reasoning would produce default
  primers as good as editorial ones.

  Risks I'd flag

  1. Quota burn — searching 8 channels × 200 archetypes × 3 formats = ~5k API
  queries, well over the free tier. Need a channel-list-once-per-day strategy:
  pull each channel's recent video list once, cache it, then match archetypes
  against the cache locally.
  2. Caption stretch — for archetypes that no creator has played recently
  (Splinter Twin, Premodern decks), this layer adds nothing. Need a graceful "no
   videos found" path.
  3. Maintenance — channels rebrand, get deleted, change naming conventions. The
   hard-coded channel list needs to be a config file you can edit without code
  changes.

  My recommendation

  Worth planning around — yes. Not as a replacement for Cards Realm but as an
  enrichment pass that fills the exact gaps (sequencing nuance, in-game matchup
  reasoning) where our current pipeline is weakest. The transcript layer is
  independent enough that it can be built without disturbing the existing primer
   orchestrator, and it has the side benefit of providing training data for a
  future custom primer-builder model.

  If you want, I can sketch a concrete plan for it once the current Modern build
   finishes — file layout, dependencies, the enrichment-merge logic, a focused
  extraction prompt, and a quota-conscious discovery strategy.

● Updated plan
  ⎿  /plan to preview

● Plan saved to /home/lou/.claude/plans/youtube-piloting-enrichment.md. Here's
  the shape:

  Architecture decision: enrichment layer, not a primary provider. Runs after
  the orchestrator builds the base guide, pulls 2–3 recent gameplay videos per
  archetype, extracts piloting heuristics, and merges them into the existing
  guide's sequencing_tips / mulligan.examples / matchups fields. Each piece gets
   its own provenance entry pointing at a YouTube URL + timestamp range, and a
  new EvidenceKind.GAMEPLAY_OBSERVED between EXPLICIT and INFERRED.

  Quota strategy: discovery is purely local once channel video lists are cached.
   Daily build_youtube_cache.py pulls ~80 units/channel × 10 channels = ~800
  units/day, well under the 10k free tier. The hot path (enriching individual
  archetypes) hits zero quota. Transcripts via youtube-transcript-api aren't
  subject to the Data API quota at all and we cache permanently.

  Caption garble handling: the extraction prompt gets the archetype's
  signature_cards list and is told explicitly "auto-captions mangle names — if
  you see 'flog' in an energy context, that's Phlage." The model handles this
  well when primed.

  Schema impact is small: one new enum value (GAMEPLAY_OBSERVED), one optional
  field on Provenance (transcript_timestamp_range). v1 guides still load
  unchanged.

  Hidden upside the plan calls out: once the corpus has 200+ archetypes' worth
  of transcript-extracted reasoning paired with their primers, that's exactly
  the training data needed for the user's earlier "primer-builder agent" idea —
  the long-term play is to fine-tune a custom default-primer model on this
  corpus.

  Initial channel list (per our discussion): AspiringSpike, Crokeyz, Jim Davis,
  Reid Duke, AndreaMengucci, mengu, DotPMtg, SpikeyMikey13, NumotTheNummy,
  Saffron Olive, PleasantKenobi. LSV deprioritized (mostly Limited).

  Rollout in 4 phases: start with 3 channels + Modern only to validate quality,
  then expand channels + formats, then schedule daily cache rebuild, then the
  training-dataset payoff.

  Plan covers files to create, files to modify, schema delta, quota math,
  failure modes, and a verification checklist. Want me to refine any section
  before we move toward implementation, or are there other angles you want
  covered (e.g. handling specific creators' formats, tournament VOD coverage,
  hooks into the runtime prompt to surface video citations)?

● Implementation complete. All 80 tests pass. Here's what shipped and how to
  bootstrap:

  Files created

  - app/knowledge/primers/youtube/ package: cache.py, match_parse.py,
  discover.py, transcripts.py, extract.py, enricher.py, api_client.py,
  channels.json
  - scripts/build_youtube_cache.py — daily channel-list refresh, quota-aware
  - scripts/enrich_piloting_guides.py — walks a piloting// dir and enriches
  every guide
  - tests/test_youtube_{match_parse,discover,enricher,transcripts}.py — 25 tests
  - cache/youtube/{channels,transcripts}/ directories (gitignored)

  Files modified

  - piloting_schema.py — added EvidenceKind.GAMEPLAY_OBSERVED and
  Provenance.transcript_timestamp_range, Provenance.extracted_for_archetype
  - scripts/build_piloting_guides.py — added --enrich-from-youtube flag
  - pyproject.toml — added youtube-transcript-api, google-api-python-client
  - .gitignore — added cache/, logs/

  Architecture decisions

  - Enrichment layer, not a primary provider — base guides stay structural,
  transcript heuristics ride alongside with kind=GAMEPLAY_OBSERVED evidence
  - Two channel kinds: creator (individual gameplay) and tournament (Play MTG —
  one video enriches two archetypes)
  - Quota path: only build_youtube_cache.py hits the YouTube Data API.
  Enrichment is purely local cache reads. ~800 units/day for the default
  10-channel list (free tier is 10k)
  - Transcripts via youtube-transcript-api — no API key, no quota, permanent
  cache
  - Caption garble correction — the extractor prompt receives signature_cards
  and is told "if you see 'flog' near energy context, that's Phlage"
  - Per-archetype tournament enrichment — same Play MTG video enriches both
  decks featured, each gets its own extraction pass with the opponent name as
  context

  How to bootstrap (you need to run these)

  # 1. Get a YouTube Data API v3 key from console.cloud.google.com
  #    (free tier; no credit card needed for ≤10k units/day)
  export YOUTUBE_API_KEY="..."

  # 2. Resolve handle → channel_id (one-time; writes back to channels.json)
  .venv/bin/python scripts/build_youtube_cache.py --resolve-only

  # 3. Fetch each channel's last 200 videos into the cache (~800 quota units)
  .venv/bin/python scripts/build_youtube_cache.py

  # 4. Enrich one archetype as a smoke test
  .venv/bin/python scripts/enrich_piloting_guides.py modern --archetype "Boros 
  Energy"

  # 5. Enrich everything in Modern
  .venv/bin/python scripts/enrich_piloting_guides.py modern

  # 6. Schedule daily: cron entry calls build_youtube_cache.py, then weekly
  #    enrich_piloting_guides.py per format (or use the new 
  --enrich-from-youtube
  #    flag on build_piloting_guides.py so the base build does both)

  What you'll see after enrichment

  Each enriched guide gains:
  - New entries in sequencing_tips with FieldEvidence{kind: gameplay_observed, 
  evidence_span: "12:34-13:00", source_index: N} pointing at a YouTube URL
  - New matchups[].advice segments tagged (from gameplay) with timestamp
  evidence
  - New mulligan.examples from observed mulligan walkthroughs
  - New notes on key_cards from creator commentary
  - One Provenance entry per video used, with publisher: "YouTube/<channel>",
  source_url, extracted_for_archetype, and used_for_fields listing what it
  contributed

  Known gaps (not blocking)

  - The smoke test of actually pulling video data needs your API key. The no-key
   path (no cache, no enrichment) is verified to be a clean no-op.
  - Resolving channel IDs for @AspiringSpike, @JimDavisMTG etc. may fail for
  handles that have changed — build_youtube_cache.py --resolve-only reports
  which ones it couldn't find, then you can fix the handles in channels.json by
  hand.

❯ We should also only get the youtube videos that have the games we are looking for, not just the content creators last 200 videos. Just making sure you are doing that 

● To answer your question directly: yes, the per-archetype filtering happens at 
  lookup time in discover.find_videos. The cache holds raw channel metadata (200
   videos per channel, ~2 KB each = trivial disk) because the quota cost is
  fixed per fetch regardless of filtering, and caching all of it lets us look up
   any archetype later for free. At query time, _match_creator requires the
  archetype tokens AND the format keyword in title/description before a video
  becomes a candidate; _match_tournament parses the title/description for two
  featured archetypes and only matches when the requested archetype is one of
  them.

  But the Play MTG investigation just surfaced a much bigger issue worth 
  flagging:

  Of 400 Play MTG videos:
  - 234 are feature matches — title is "Semifinal | Larsen vs. Zhang | Standard 
  | #PTSOS". The archetype names are NOT in the title or description. The
  description just has timestamps + a link to magic.gg.
  - 8 are deck techs — these DO name the archetype: "Javier Dominguez | Modern 
  Deck Tech | Mono-Green Tron | ..."
  - 158 are non-match content (Strixhaven set hype, Lofi study videos, etc.)
  - Of the deck techs, only 1 matches a current Modern archetype.

  So Play MTG's high-signal feature-match content is unreachable from YouTube
  metadata alone — you'd need to cross-reference magic.gg/events/<event>
  decklist pages to learn which player played which deck in which round. That's
  a separate scrape and was out of scope for v1.

  What does work well today:
  - Creator channels: AspiringSpike, Crokeyz, Jim Davis, Andrea Mengucci,
  PleasantKenobi (5 channels × 200 videos = 1000 cached videos, filtered
  per-archetype at query time)
  - Play MTG deck tech videos (small but high-quality)

  Two paths from here. Tell me which you want:

  1. Ship v1 now with creator channels only (and the handful of Play MTG deck
  techs that match by archetype name). Run the smoke test, kick off the format
  builds, get something working end-to-end.
  2. Add magic.gg deck-roster scraping first so Play MTG feature matches become
  usable. Roughly: scrape magic.gg/events/<slug> → mapping of {player_name: 
  archetype, round_num: video_id} → join into the YouTube cache. Probably 1-2
  hours of work; pushes v1 ship.

  Which way?

✻ Cogitated for 1m 56s

❯ is adding magic.gg deck-roster scraping first really the best way? What are   
  our other options, I guess we would have to get the actual content of each    
  youtube video script to know what decks are being played. I would want to do  
  the magic.gg deck-roster scraping first, as the Play MTG feature matches      
  provide valuable information                                                  

● Honest take: transcript-based archetype identification is probably better than
   magic.gg scraping, and you raised the right question. Let me lay it out:

  Option D: transcript card-name matching (self-contained)

  The insight: commentators say card names constantly during gameplay. If we
  pull a Play MTG match transcript and string-match against the signature cards
  from our metagame data, we get archetype identification for free.

  Example: a Modern semifinal transcript probably mentions "Phlage" 8×, "Guide
  of Souls" 12×, "Ragavan" 6× → strong Boros Energy signal. And "Force of
  Negation" 9×, "Living End" 11×, "Subtlety" 4× → strong Living End signal. Two
  archetypes pass the threshold → this is a Boros Energy vs. Living End feature
  match.

  Why this beats magic.gg:
  - No extra scraper to maintain. Magic.gg is Wizards' marketing site — they
  redesign it constantly.
  - No site-structure dependency. We already need to fetch transcripts for the
  LLM extraction; this just adds a cheap pre-pass.
  - Works for any tournament VOD channel, not just Play MTG. (CFB's channel,
  Sneaky Bone Mage, any future addition.)
  - Caption garbles don't matter much when you're scoring across 5-10 signature
  cards — a few mishearings won't move the count below threshold.
  - Zero YouTube API quota cost. Transcripts are free.

  What it costs:
  - One transcript fetch per Play MTG match video. ~234 fetches × ~3s each = ~12
   min one-time, then cached forever.
  - Threshold tuning: how many distinct signature cards from one archetype need
  to appear before we tag the video? Probably 4-5.

  Where it's weaker than magic.gg:
  - Doesn't give us decklists, just archetype labels. (For our use case —
  enrichment — we don't need full decklists, the archetype name is what merges
  into the matchup field.)
  - A new archetype that emerged post-tournament won't get tagged retroactively
  until we re-scan. (Easy to handle: re-scan when metagame_data updates.)
  - If commentary references a card but the deck isn't actually playing it (e.g.
   "I wish I had a Force of Negation here"), we get noise. Solved by requiring
  multiple distinct signature cards, not just one.

  Other options ranked

  Approach: D: transcript signature-card matching
  Reliability: High
  Maintenance: Low (uses data we already have)
  Effort: ~2 hours
  Verdict: Recommended
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Approach: A: magic.gg event-page scrape
  Reliability: High
  Maintenance: Medium-high (HTML changes)
  Effort: ~2-3 hours
  Verdict: Backup if D ambiguous
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Approach: Hybrid D→A fallback
  Reliability: Highest
  Maintenance: Medium
  Effort: ~3-4 hours
  Verdict: Best long-term
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Approach: B: LLM identifies decks from transcript
  Reliability: High
  Maintenance: None
  Effort: ~1 hour
  Verdict: Expensive — wastes LLM on already-solved problem
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Approach: C: video description / mtgmelee / mtgtop8
  Reliability: Inconsistent
  Maintenance: High
  Effort: ~3 hours
  Verdict: Description doesn't have it; mtgmelee is sparse for paper events

  My recommendation

  Implement Option D as the primary tournament identifier. It's self-contained,
  cheap, and uses data we already have to maintain (metagame_data +
  signature_cards). Save magic.gg as a v2 enhancement when we hit a case where
  transcript matching is ambiguous (1 deck identified, or 3+ candidates above
  threshold) — at that point we'll know the failure modes and the scraper can be
   narrowly targeted.

  The implementation is basically: add a youtube/match_identify.py module with a
   identify_archetypes_from_transcript(transcript_text, 
  all_archetypes_with_signature_cards) -> list[(archetype, score)] function, and
   have discover._match_tournament call it when the title/description-based
  parser returns nothing.

  Want me to go with Option D, or do you still want magic.gg first? I genuinely
  think D is the cleaner play here.

       5  chunks because isolated 2-second chunks lose context.

       7  Transcripts are cached permanently — captions don't change.
       8 +                                                               
       9 +Rate limiting:                                                 
      10 +  * Enforces a min interval between fetches (default 3.5s, over
         +ride with                                                      
      11 +    ``YOUTUBE_TRANSCRIPT_MIN_INTERVAL``).                      
      12 +  * On IpBlocked, applies exponential backoff (60s → 300s → 900
         +s, capped).                                                    
      13 +  * After 3 consecutive IpBlocked errors, fetches stop returnin
         +g None                                                         
      14 +    instead of retrying — the caller can resume later from the 
         +cache.                                                         
      15  """
      16  
      17  from __future__ import annotations
      18  
      19  import logging
      20 +import os                                                      
      21 +import random                                                  
      22 +import threading                                               
      23 +import time                                                    
      24  from dataclasses import dataclass
      25  from typing import Optional
      26  
     ...
      28  
      29  log = logging.getLogger(__name__)
      30  
      31 +# Throttle: minimum seconds between consecutive transcript fetc
         +hes.                                                           
      32 +_MIN_FETCH_INTERVAL = float(os.environ.get("YOUTUBE_TRANSCRIPT_
         +MIN_INTERVAL", "3.5"))                                         
      33 +# IpBlocked backoff schedule: each entry is the sleep BEFORE th
         +e next attempt.                                                
      34 +_IP_BLOCK_BACKOFF = [60.0, 300.0, 900.0]                       
      35 +# After this many consecutive IpBlocked failures, stop returnin
         +g real fetches.                                                
      36 +_IP_BLOCK_HARD_STOP = 3                                        
      37  
      38 +# Module-level rate-limit state. Locked so multiple threads (if
         + any) don't race.                                              
      39 +_state_lock = threading.Lock()                                 
      40 +_last_fetch_time: float = 0.0                                  
      41 +_consecutive_ip_blocks: int = 0                                
      42 +                                                               
      43 +                                                               
      44 +def _throttle() -> None:                                       
      45 +    """Sleep so consecutive fetches are at least _MIN_FETCH_INT
         +ERVAL apart."""                                                
      46 +    global _last_fetch_time                                    
      47 +    with _state_lock:                                          
      48 +        now = time.monotonic()                                 
      49 +        wait = _MIN_FETCH_INTERVAL - (now - _last_fetch_time)  
      50 +        if wait > 0:                                           
      51 +            # Add a small jitter so we don't synchronize on the
         + boundary.                                                     
      52 +            wait += random.uniform(0, 0.5)                     
      53 +            time.sleep(wait)                                   
      54 +        _last_fetch_time = time.monotonic()                    
      55 +                                                               
      56 +                                                               
      57 +def _is_ip_blocked(exc: Exception) -> bool:                    
      58 +    name = type(exc).__name__                                  
      59 +    return "IpBlocked" in name or "IPBlocked" in name          
      60 +                                                               
      61 +                                                               
      62 +def _register_ip_block() -> int:                               
      63 +    global _consecutive_ip_blocks                              
      64 +    with _state_lock:                                          
      65 +        _consecutive_ip_blocks += 1                            
      66 +        return _consecutive_ip_blocks                          
      67 +                                                               
      68 +                                                               
      69 +def _register_ok() -> None:                                    
      70 +    global _consecutive_ip_blocks                              
      71 +    with _state_lock:                                          
      72 +        _consecutive_ip_blocks = 0                             
      73 +                                                               
      74 +                                                               
      75 +def ip_block_hard_stop() -> bool:                              
      76 +    """True when we've hit too many consecutive IpBlocked error
         +s."""                                                          
      77 +    with _state_lock:                                          
      78 +        return _consecutive_ip_blocks >= _IP_BLOCK_HARD_STOP   
      79 +                                                               
      80 +                                                               
      81  @dataclass(slots=True)
      82  class TranscriptChunk:
      83      start_sec: float

✻ Churned for 2m 14s

❯ are you using my youtube data v3 api key? why are you getting ipblocked       
  backoffs?                                                                     

● Honest answer: the API key isn't used for transcripts — only for channel/video
   metadata. Let me explain the distinction because it's worth knowing.

  YouTube exposes captions through two paths:

  Path: YouTube Data API v3 (your key)
  Auth: API key OR OAuth
  Quota: 10k units/day
  What it does: Channel info, video lists, view counts. captions.download 
    requires OAuth + the video owner's permission — only works for videos you
    own.
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Path: youtube-transcript-api library
  Auth: None
  Quota: None official
  What it does: Scrapes the public caption endpoint that browsers hit.
  Anonymous.
    No API key needed, no quota. But because it's anonymous, YouTube  applies 
    anti-abuse rate limiting based on IP.

  So our pipeline uses the API key for the things it can do (resolving handles,
  listing channel uploads, fetching view counts — all working fine), and
  youtube-transcript-api for transcripts because there's no key-authenticated
  alternative for third-party video captions. The IpBlocked errors are YouTube's
   anti-scrape measures kicking in on the anonymous endpoint.

  Quick check on the actual log:

❯ where can i check the data in the primers? tell me the command                
● Where to find the data

  Files live as JSON under
  forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/piloting/<format>/<slug>.json. So for example:

  # List all built guides
  ls forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/piloting/modern/
  ls forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/piloting/pioneer/

  # Read one raw
  less forge-llm-sidecar/app/knowledge/piloting/modern/boros-energy.json

  A pretty-printer for quick review

  The Python one-liner I used earlier renders a single guide nicely. Save it
  once and reuse:

  # View any one guide in human-readable form
  cd /home/lou/Development/forge-1/forge-llm-sidecar
  .venv/bin/python -c "
  import json, sys, textwrap
  from pathlib import Path
  fmt, slug = sys.argv[1], sys.argv[2]
  g = json.load(open(f'app/knowledge/piloting/{fmt}/{slug}.json'))
  print(f'=== {g[\"archetype\"]}  ({g[\"metadata\"][\"source\"]}) ===')
  print('STRATEGY:', g['strategy_type'])
  print()
  print('OVERVIEW:')
  print(textwrap.fill(g.get('overview',''), 100))
  print()
  for label, key in [('WIN CONDITIONS','win_conditions'),
                      ('SEQUENCING TIPS','sequencing_tips'),
                      ('COMMON THREATS','common_threats')]:
      if g.get(key):
          print(f'{label}:')
          for x in g[key]: print(f'  - {x}')
          print()
  for k in ('keep_criteria','mulligan_criteria'):
      if g['mulligan'].get(k):
          print(f'MULLIGAN {k.upper()}:')
          for x in g['mulligan'][k]: print(f'  - {x}')
          print()
  if g.get('key_cards'):
      print('KEY CARDS:')
      for c in g['key_cards']:
          print(f'  - {c[\"name\"]} — {c.get(\"role\",\"\")}')
          if c.get('notes'): print(f'      {c[\"notes\"]}')
      print()
  if g.get('matchups'):
      print('MATCHUPS:')
      for m in g['matchups']:
          print(f'  vs {m[\"opponent_archetype\"]}: {m.get(\"advice\",\"\")}')
          if m.get('watch_for'): print(f'     watch: {\", 
  \".join(m[\"watch_for\"])}')
      print()
  print('PROVENANCE:', [p.get('publisher') for p in g.get('provenance',[])])
  " modern boros-energy

  Replace modern boros-energy at the end with whatever format + slug you want.

  Or use the sidecar's debug endpoint

  If the sidecar is running, you can also hit:

  curl 'http://localhost:8080/piloting?format=modern&archetype=Boros%20Energy' |
   jq
  curl 'http://localhost:8080/piloting?format=pioneer' | jq    # lists all 
  available

  (That endpoint also surfaces stale_flags computed against
  banlist_events.json.)

  What got added (the good)

  - New vs Azorius Control matchup: specific PT MH3-derived advice — "Use Force
  of Negation to counter Cord of Calling and Solitude to counter Nadu while it
  is on the stack", "Include Dress Down to temporarily remove Nadu's abilities",
   "Sun Cleanser is highly effective against the energy package because it
  removes all energy counters". All tagged (from gameplay).
  - Force of Negation note: appended usage from real play — "Used to counter key
   combo pieces on the stack to prevent the opponent from drawing cards"
  - Subtlety note: appended — "Bypasses certain stack-based protections in games
   one and two, requiring direct answers rather than relying on stack
  manipulation effects"

  What broke (the bad)

  Issue 1 — duplicated provenance. The 3 Play MTG videos appear twice in
  provenance (entries 2-4 and 5-7 are identical URLs). The smoke-test enrichment
   from yesterday added them, then today's full Modern enrichment re-added them
  without dedup. The _seq_tip_exists check only dedupes sequencing tips, not
  provenance + key-card notes (so those got the "from gameplay" suffix tacked on
   twice as well).

  Issue 2 — opponent name mis-attribution. The matchup is labelled "vs Azorius
  Control" but the advice references Bant Nadu ("Nadu while it is on the stack",
   "the control list is specifically tuned to beat Bant Nadu"). Looking at PT
  MH3 metagame: Living End was playing against Bant Nadu, not Azorius Control.
  The transcript signature-card identifier mis-tagged a Bant Nadu video as
  Azorius Control because both decks share Force of Negation + Solitude +
  Subtlety signatures. The high-confidence card overlap caused a false ID.

  Want me to fix one or both:
  1. Add provenance dedup to the enricher (cheap, ~10 lines — hashes by
  source_url + extracted_for_archetype)
  2. Tighten archetype identification — require not just N distinct signature
  cards but at least one unique (not shared with the other top candidate)
  signature card. E.g. Bant Nadu would need "Nadu" itself for confidence ≥ 0.7,
  not just shared Force/Solitude. Bigger change but addresses the root cause.

  unique_distinct=1. So at least one card unique to Azorius Control's sig list
  (likely Supreme Verdict or Teferi, Time Raveler) IS being mentioned. Looking
  at our earlier Living End diff: the LLM said "this control list is tuned to
  beat Bant Nadu" — that means the actual opposing deck was Azorius Control, and
   the commentators were discussing how it was configured against Bant Nadu. The
   original identification was correct after all. My earlier concern about it
  being a false positive was misreading the LLM output.

  Living End now has 7 Play MTG identifications (down from 8), all with
  unique_distinct=1 for Living End — solid confidence.

  The new uniqueness scoring is working as designed, just stricter than I
  initially calibrated. The 4 lost archetypes (Mardu Energy / Blink decks) are
  debatable losses — their signatures genuinely overlap with other archetypes.

● The verification revealed real findings. Three things stand out:

  1. Most "Azorius Control" matches are the SAME player

  Francisco Sánchez piloted his Azorius Control (Tameshi build) deep into PT EOE
   — Quarterfinal, Semifinal, Final, plus Round 16. So the "12 Azorius Control
  matches" isn't 12 different decks, it's 1 player appearing as the opponent in 
  many feature matches. Each transcript mentions his cards (Teferi, Narset,
  Orim's Chant, Isochron Scepter), so signature-card matching keeps tagging him.

  That's actually... correct behavior. Just inflated by player concentration in
  feature matches.

  2. There ARE real misidentifications

  Video: Round 14: Nakamura vs Schabel
  Our cache says: Affinity + Azorius Control
  LLM verdict: Affinity + Izzet Prowess
  Truth: Schabel was playing Cori-Steel Cutter + Slickshot Show-Off + Lightning
    Bolt — definitely Izzet Prowess, not Azorius
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Video: Round 16: Guttman vs Garcia
  Our cache says: Azorius Control + Esper Murktide
  LLM verdict: Goryo's Vengeance + Jeskai Control
  Truth: Goryo's Vengeance card itself + Atraxa Grand Unifier in the transcript
  —
    Goryo was missed
  ────────────────────────────────────────
  Video: Final: Sánchez vs DeBenedetto-Plummer
  Our cache says: Jeskai + Azorius
  LLM verdict: Belcher + Jeskai Control
  Truth: DBP was playing Tameshi Belchure (Lotus Bloom + Goblin Charbelcher) —
    Belcher isn't in our metagame_data

  So the LLM verification is genuinely catching false positives our
  signature-card heuristic missed.

  3. The Jeskai vs Azorius distinction is uncertain

  The LLM repeatedly overrides the commentators' "Azorius Control" label and
  says "Jeskai Control" because both archetypes share Teferi/Narset/Orim's Chant
   in their signature lists. Without seeing the actual decklists on magic.gg, I
  can't say which one is more accurate. The commentators on a Wizards channel
  would know — but our LLM doesn't trust them when its sig-list matching
  disagrees.

  What this implies for the enrichment data

  Real risks worth flagging:
  - The "vs Azorius Control" matchup entries on Affinity / Living End / Amulet
  Titan / etc. guides MIGHT be Jeskai Control instead — or might be correct,
  depending on what the actual decklists were
  - The "vs Esper Murktide" match in Living End might actually be Jeskai Control
  - The Affinity enrichment paired Affinity with Azorius Control but the actual
  opponent (in at least one of those) was Izzet Prowess

  Three ways to fix

  A) Add the missing archetypes to metagame_data — add Tameshi Belcher, expand
  Izzet Prowess signatures to be unique enough (Cori-Steel Cutter + Slickshot
  Show-Off + Monastery Swiftspear together)

  B) Make LLM verification a built-in step — after signature-card
  identification, run the LLM check on each result; trust the LLM's verdict when
   it disagrees and confidently names a different archetype that's in our
  metagame

  C) Cross-reference with magic.gg event coverage — the deck assignments are
  there for every PT match; would settle these questions definitively

  What do you want? My recommendation: B for now (built-in verification step
  using LLM, reusing this script's logic), since we already have the LLM and the
   cached transcripts; A as a maintenance pass when you spot specific gaps; C as
   a future improvement when the corpus expands.

  --verify-with-llm.

          + list[dict]) -> str:

      217 +        f"- {a['name']}: " + ", ".join((a.get("signature_cards
          +") or [])[:10])

      247 +def verify_with_llm(                                          
      248 +    transcript_text: str,                                     
      249 +    archetypes: list[dict],                                   
      250 +    *,                                                        
      251 +    fmt: str,                                                 
      252 +    initial_scores: list["ArchetypeScore"] | None = None,     
      253 +) -> dict | None:                                             
      254 +    """Ask the builder LLM to identify both players' decks fro
          +m a transcript.                                               
      255 +                                                              
      256 +    Returns the LLM's JSON verdict or None on failure. Caller 
          +decides whether                                               
      257 +    to override signature-card identifications based on this. 
      258 +                                                              
      259 +    ``initial_scores`` is informational — included so the prom
          +pt has                                                        
      260 +    additional context if needed.                             
      261 +    """                                                       
      262 +    from app.knowledge import builder_llm                     
      263 +                                                              
      264 +    try:                                                      
      265 +        return builder_llm.generate_guide_json(               
      266 +            _verify_prompt(transcript_text, fmt, archetypes), 
      267 +            system=_VERIFY_SYSTEM,                            
      268 +        )                                                     
      269 +    except builder_llm.BuilderLLMError as exc:                
      270 +        log.warning("verify_with_llm: LLM failed (%s)", exc)  
      271 +        return None                                           
      272 +                                                              
      273 +                                                              
      274 +def reconcile_with_llm(                                       
      275 +    sig_scores: list["ArchetypeScore"],                       
      276 +    llm_verdict: dict,                                        
      277 +    known_names: set[str],                                    
      278 +) -> tuple[list["ArchetypeScore"], list[dict]]:               
      279 +    """Merge signature-card scores with LLM verdict.          
      280 +                                                              
      281 +    Returns ``(final_scores, audit_log)``.                    
      282 +                                                              
      283 +    Rule of thumb:                                            
      284 +      - LLM names an archetype in our metagame that's NOT in s
          +ig_scores at all                                              
      285 +        → ADD that archetype with confidence from LLM (or 0.7 
          +default), tag                                                 
      286 +        ``via=llm_verification``.                             
      287 +      - LLM names a different archetype than the top signature
          +-card score AND                                               
      288 +        the LLM-named archetype is in our metagame            
      289 +        → REPLACE the top sig score with the LLM choice, tag  
      290 +        ``signature_card_guess_was`` for provenance.          
      291 +      - LLM says 'unknown' or names something not in metagame 
          +→ keep                                                        
      292 +        signature-card scores unchanged.                      
      293 +    """                                                       
      294 +    audit: list[dict] = []                                    
      295 +    if not isinstance(llm_verdict, dict):                     
      296 +        return sig_scores, audit                              
      297 +                                                              
      298 +    final: dict[str, ArchetypeScore] = {s.name: s for s in sig
          +_scores}                                                      
      299 +    sig_names = set(final.keys())                             
      300 +                                                              
      301 +    llm_archetypes: list[str] = []                            
      302 +    for side_key in ("player_a", "player_b"):                 
      303 +        side = llm_verdict.get(side_key) or {}                
      304 +        name = (side.get("archetype_guess") or "").strip()    
      305 +        if not name or name.lower() == "unknown":             
      306 +            continue                                          
      307 +        if name not in known_names:                           
      308 +            audit.append({"action": "llm_named_unknown", "name
          +": name, "side": side_key})                                   
      309 +            continue                                          
      310 +        llm_archetypes.append(name)                           
      311 +                                                              
      312 +    # If LLM lists names that aren't in sig_scores, add them. 
      313 +    for name in llm_archetypes:                               
      314 +        if name not in sig_names:                             
      315 +            # Use LLM-side confidence if present, else 0.7    
      316 +            side_a = llm_verdict.get("player_a") or {}        
      317 +            side_b = llm_verdict.get("player_b") or {}        
      318 +            llm_conf = 0.7                                    
      319 +            if side_a.get("archetype_guess") == name:         
      320 +                llm_conf = float(side_a.get("confidence") or 0
          +.7)                                                           
      321 +            elif side_b.get("archetype_guess") == name:       
      322 +                llm_conf = float(side_b.get("confidence") or 0
          +.7)                                                           
      323 +            final[name] = ArchetypeScore(                     
      324 +                name=name,                                    
      325 +                distinct_cards=0,                             
      326 +                total_mentions=0,                             
      327 +                unique_distinct=0,                            
      328 +                confidence=llm_conf,                          
      329 +            )                                                 
      330 +            audit.append({"action": "llm_added", "name": name,
          + "confidence": llm_conf})                                     
      331 +                                                              
      332 +    # If the LLM names exactly 2 archetypes and they don't inc
          +lude the                                                      
      333 +    # top sig score, REPLACE the top sig score with the LLM's 
          +choice                                                        
      334 +    # (preserving evidence the original guess was different). 
      335 +    if (                                                      
      336 +        len(llm_archetypes) == 2                              
      337 +        and sig_scores                                        
      338 +        and sig_scores[0].name not in llm_archetypes          
      339 +    ):                                                        
      340 +        rejected = sig_scores[0].name                         
      341 +        # Remove the rejected archetype                       
      342 +        final.pop(rejected, None)                             
      343 +        audit.append(                                         
      344 +            {                                                 
      345 +                "action": "llm_rejected_sig_top",             
      346 +                "rejected": rejected,                         
      347 +                "kept": llm_archetypes,                       
      348 +            }                                                 
      349 +        )                                                     
      350 +                                                              
      351 +    # Return sorted by confidence                             
      352 +    result = sorted(final.values(), key=lambda s: s.confidence
          +, reverse=True)                                               
      353 +    return result, audit                                      
      354 +                                                              
      355 +

      357      distinct: int,
      358      total: int,

  answer: in the Quarterfinal vs Buonadonna the LLM called it Jeskai Control
  (audit confirms llm_added: Jeskai Control 0.95), so Sánchez's deck was Jeskai
  across the bracket. The remaining 4 Azorius Control entries are presumably
  real Azorius Control decks (other players).

  Concrete corrections logged in audit:
  - Quarterfinal Schabel vs Horiuchi: we said "Esper Murktide vs ?" — actually
  Izzet Prowess vs Esper GenericBlink
  - Round 16 Guttman vs Garcia: we said "Azorius Control vs ?" — actually
  Goryo's Vengeance vs Jeskai Control
  - Round 8 Nakamura vs Nishi: we said "Amulet Titan vs ?" — actually Affinity
  vs Belcher

  Now what

  The cache identified_archetypes data is corrected, but the Modern guides on 
  disk still have the old (wrong) matchup advice baked in. To take advantage of
  the new identifications, we need to re-enrich. The provenance-dedup logic will
   skip videos already merged for an archetype, so to actually update we'd need
  to either:

  1. Clear the YouTube provenance + matchup text from the modern guides, then
  re-run enrichment (clean slate, picks up the corrected identifications)
  2. Just re-enrich — dedup will skip existing video/archetype pairs, but any
  NEW archetype identifications (Belcher, Izzet Prowess, etc.) will get their
  guides enriched for the first time
  3. Both — option 1 for the previously-wrong archetypes, option 2 for
  everything

  Which approach? I lean toward option 2 — leave the existing enrichments alone
  (they include some real PT content even if mis-labeled), and let the
  newly-correct identifications enrich their respective guides. We can manually
  scrub specific bad entries later if you want.

  The AI profile files (forge-gui/res/ai/*.ai) don't set any SIDECAR keys, so

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Where to apply this on your phone

  The Android Forge install reads AI profiles from a path under your phone's
  storage. Depending on Android version it's one of:

  - Android 11+ (Q+): Android/obb/forge.app.<flavor>/Forge/res/ai/Default.ai
  (the actual obb subdir is com.googleplay.forgeapp / forge.app / similar —
  check what's there)
  - Older Android: /sdcard/Forge/res/ai/Default.ai

  Open that file with a text editor on your phone (e.g. Material Files, Solid
  Explorer, or any text editor that can write to /Android/obb/) and append the
  same block:

  SIDECAR_INFLUENCE_ENABLE=true
  SIDECAR_ROLE_ASSESSMENT_ENABLE=true
  SIDECAR_HAND_VALUATION_ENABLE=true
  SIDECAR_OPPONENT_INFERENCE_ENABLE=true
  SIDECAR_TARGETING_ENABLE=true
  SIDECAR_MULLIGAN_ENABLE=true

  Then fully restart Forge (force-stop and re-launch — AI profiles load at
  startup) and start a new constructed match.

  What to expect after the restart

  The sidecar log should start showing hits to:
  - POST /identify-own-archetype — once per game when Forge starts
  - POST /recognize — periodically as the human opponent plays cards
  - POST /forge-log/analyze — on certain board state events

  If you start a game and STILL don't see those, the diagnosis path is:
  1. Check that AiController.java is actually instantiated (i.e. AI is your
  opponent and isn't suppressed in adventure mode etc.)
  2. Tail the Forge app log on Android for SidecarInfluence / SidecarClient
  errors
  3. Tail this sidecar's log (tail -F 
  /home/lou/Development/forge-1/forge-llm-sidecar/logs/sidecar.log) for
  connection attempts

  Let me know what you see after the restart.
